2025-11-01 11:37:12.616 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:170 - ## Code: main.py
```python
## main.py
from typing import List

def has_close_elements(numbers: List[float], threshold: float) -> bool:
    """ Check if in given list of numbers, are any two numbers closer to each other than given threshold.
    
    Args:
        numbers: List of float numbers to check.
        threshold: A float value representing the threshold distance.
        
    Returns:
        True if any two numbers are closer than threshold, otherwise False.
        
    Examples:
        >>> has_close_elements([1.0, 2.0, 3.0], 0.5)
        False
        >>> has_close_elements([1.0, 2.8, 3.0, 4.0, 5.0, 2.0], 0.3)
        True
    """
    # Sort the list of numbers to enable adjacent comparison
    sorted_numbers = sorted(numbers)
    
    # Iterate through the sorted list and check adjacent pairs
    for i in range(len(sorted_numbers) - 1):
        if sorted_numbers[i + 1] - sorted_numbers[i] < threshold:
            return True
            
    return False
```

2025-11-01 11:47:28.151 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:170 - ## Code: main.py
```python
## main.py
from typing import List

def has_close_elements(numbers: List[float], threshold: float) -> bool:
    """Check if any two numbers in the list are closer than the specified threshold.

    Args:
        numbers (List[float]): A list of floating-point numbers.
        threshold (float): The threshold distance to check against.

    Returns:
        bool: True if any two numbers are closer than the threshold, False otherwise.
    """
    # Handle edge cases: empty list or list with a single element
    if len(numbers) < 2:
        return False

    # Sort the numbers to make it easier to find close elements
    sorted_numbers = sorted(numbers)

    # Iterate through the sorted list and check the difference between consecutive elements
    for i in range(len(sorted_numbers) - 1):
        if sorted_numbers[i + 1] - sorted_numbers[i] < threshold:
            return True

    return False
```

2025-11-01 11:56:10.398 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:170 - ## Code: main.py
```python
## main.py
from typing import List

def has_close_elements(numbers: List[float], threshold: float) -> bool:
    """ 检查给定数字列表中是否有任何两个数字的差值小于给定的阈值。
    
    :param numbers: 包含浮点数的列表
    :param threshold: 浮点数，表示阈值
    :return: 如果存在两个数字的差值小于阈值，则返回True，否则返回False
    
    >>> has_close_elements([1.0, 2.0, 3.0], 0.5)
    False
    >>> has_close_elements([1.0, 2.8, 3.0, 4.0, 5.0, 2.0], 0.3)
    True
    """
    if len(numbers) < 2:
        return False  # 如果列表为空或只有一个元素，返回False

    # 对列表进行排序以便于比较
    sorted_numbers = sorted(numbers)

    # 遍历排序后的列表，检查相邻元素的差值
    for i in range(len(sorted_numbers) - 1):
        if sorted_numbers[i + 1] - sorted_numbers[i] < threshold:
            return True  # 找到两个数字的差值小于阈值

    return False  # 没有找到符合条件的数字对
```

2025-11-01 12:01:52.513 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:170 - ## Code: main.py
```python
## main.py
from typing import List

def has_close_elements(numbers: List[float], threshold: float) -> bool:
    """ 检查给定数字列表中是否有任何两个数字的差值小于给定的阈值。
    
    :param numbers: 包含浮点数的列表
    :param threshold: 浮点数，表示阈值
    :return: 如果存在两个数字的差值小于阈值，则返回True，否则返回False
    
    >>> has_close_elements([1.0, 2.0, 3.0], 0.5)
    False
    >>> has_close_elements([1.0, 2.8, 3.0, 4.0, 5.0, 2.0], 0.3)
    True
    """
    # 处理边缘情况
    if len(numbers) < 2:
        return False

    # 对列表进行排序以便于比较
    sorted_numbers = sorted(numbers)

    # 检查相邻元素的差值
    for i in range(len(sorted_numbers) - 1):
        if sorted_numbers[i + 1] - sorted_numbers[i] < threshold:
            return True

    return False
```

2025-11-01 12:44:28.246 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:170 - ## Code: main.py
```python
## main.py
from typing import List

def has_close_elements(numbers: List[float], threshold: float) -> bool:
    """检查给定数字列表中是否有任何两个数字之间的差值小于给定的阈值。
    
    :param numbers: List[float] - 浮点数列表
    :param threshold: float - 阈值
    :return: bool - 如果存在两个数字之间的差值小于阈值，则返回True，否则返回False
    
    >>> has_close_elements([1.0, 2.0, 3.0], 0.5)
    False
    >>> has_close_elements([1.0, 2.8, 3.0, 4.0, 5.0, 2.0], 0.3)
    True
    """
    # Sort the list to make it easier to find close elements
    sorted_numbers = sorted(numbers)
    
    # Check the difference between consecutive elements
    for i in range(len(sorted_numbers) - 1):
        if abs(sorted_numbers[i] - sorted_numbers[i + 1]) < threshold:
            return True
            
    return False
```

2025-11-01 12:56:53.458 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:170 - ## Code: test.py
```python
## test.py

from typing import List

def has_close_elements(numbers: List[float], threshold: float) -> bool:
    """Check if any two numbers in the list are closer than the specified threshold.

    Parameters:
    numbers (List[float]): The list of numbers to check.
    threshold (float): The threshold distance to compare.

    Returns:
    bool: True if any two numbers are closer than the threshold, False otherwise.
    """
    # Handle edge cases
    if len(numbers) < 2:
        return False  # Less than two elements cannot be close

    # Sort the numbers to make it easier to find close elements
    sorted_numbers = sorted(numbers)

    # Check for close elements
    for i in range(len(sorted_numbers) - 1):
        if sorted_numbers[i + 1] - sorted_numbers[i] < threshold:
            return True  # Found two close elements

    return False  # No close elements found
```

2025-11-01 13:08:01.975 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:170 - ## Code: main.py
```python
## main.py
from typing import List

def has_close_elements(numbers: List[float], threshold: float) -> bool:
    """Check if any two numbers in the list are closer than the specified threshold.

    Args:
        numbers (List[float]): A list of floating-point numbers.
        threshold (float): The threshold distance to check against.

    Returns:
        bool: True if any two numbers are closer than the threshold, False otherwise.
    """
    # Handle edge cases
    if len(numbers) < 2:
        return False

    # Sort the numbers to make it easier to find close elements
    sorted_numbers = sorted(numbers)

    # Iterate through the sorted list and check the difference between consecutive elements
    for i in range(len(sorted_numbers) - 1):
        if sorted_numbers[i + 1] - sorted_numbers[i] < threshold:
            return True

    return False
```

2025-11-01 13:14:06.915 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:169 - in aasking LLM, output is: 
2025-11-01 13:14:06.915 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:170 - ## Code: main.py
```python
## main.py
from typing import List

def has_close_elements(numbers: List[float], threshold: float) -> bool:
    """Check if any two numbers in the list are closer than the specified threshold.

    Args:
        numbers (List[float]): A list of floating-point numbers.
        threshold (float): The threshold distance to check against.

    Returns:
        bool: True if any two numbers are closer than the threshold, False otherwise.
    """
    # Handle edge cases: empty list or list with a single element
    if len(numbers) < 2:
        return False

    # Sort the numbers to make it easier to find close elements
    sorted_numbers = sorted(numbers)

    # Iterate through the sorted list and check the difference between consecutive elements
    for i in range(len(sorted_numbers) - 1):
        if sorted_numbers[i + 1] - sorted_numbers[i] < threshold:
            return True

    return False
```

def has_close_elements(numbers: List[float], threshold: float) -> bool:
    """ Check if in given list of numbers, are any two numbers closer to each other than
    given threshold.
    >>> has_close_elements([1.0, 2.0, 3.0], 0.5)

2025-11-01 13:38:02.556 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:170 - ## Code: main.py
```python
## main.py
from typing import List

def has_close_elements(numbers: List[float], threshold: float) -> bool:
    """检查给定数字列表中是否有任何两个数字之间的差值小于给定的阈值。
    
    参数：
    numbers: List[float] - 浮点数列表
    threshold: float - 阈值
    
    返回：
    bool - 如果存在两个数字之间的差值小于阈值，则返回True，否则返回False。
    
    示例：
    >>> has_close_elements([1.0, 2.0, 3.0], 0.5)
    False
    >>> has_close_elements([1.0, 2.8, 3.0, 4.0, 5.0, 2.0], 0.3)
    True
    """
    # 对数字进行排序，以便可以高效地检查相邻元素
    numbers.sort()
    
    # 遍历排序后的列表，检查相邻元素之间的差值
    for i in range(len(numbers) - 1):
        if abs(numbers[i] - numbers[i + 1]) < threshold:
            return True
            
    return False
```

2025-11-01 13:38:23.349 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:170 - ## Code: main.py
```python
## main.py

from typing import List

def identify_non_prime_numbers(numbers: List[int]) -> List[int]:
    """Identify non-prime numbers from a list.

    Parameters:
    numbers (List[int]): A list of integers to check.

    Returns:
    List[int]: A list of non-prime integers.
    """
    non_prime_numbers = []
    
    for number in numbers:
        if not is_prime(number):
            non_prime_numbers.append(number)
    
    return non_prime_numbers

def is_prime(n: int) -> bool:
    """Check if a number is prime.

    Parameters:
    n (int): The number to check.

    Returns:
    bool: True if the number is prime, False otherwise.
    """
    if n <= 1:
        return False
    for i in range(2, int(n**0.5) + 1):
        if n % i == 0:
            return False
    return True
```

2025-11-01 18:03:40.087 | INFO     | metagpt.provider.base_llm:aask:170 - ## Code: main.py
```python
## main.py

from typing import List

def make_a_pile(n: int) -> List[int]:
    """ 
    Given a positive integer n, generates a list of stone levels.
    The first level has n stones.
    The next level has the next odd number if n is odd, or the next even number if n is even.
    Returns a list where element at index i represents the number of stones in level (i+1).

    Args:
        n (int): A positive integer representing the number of levels.

    Returns:
        List[int]: A list of integers representing the number of stones in each level.

    Raises:
        ValueError: If n is not a positive integer.

    Examples:
        >>> make_a_pile(3)
        [3, 5, 7]
        >>> make_a_pile(4)
        [4, 6, 8]
    """
    if n <= 0:
        raise ValueError("Input must be a positive integer.")

    stone_levels = [n]  # Initialize the list with the first level

    for i in range(1, n):  # Loop for levels from 1 to n-1
        if stone_levels[i - 1] % 2 == 0:  # Check if the last level is even
            next_stone_count = stone_levels[i - 1] + 2  # Next even number
        else:
            next_stone_count = stone_levels[i - 1] + 2  # Next odd number

        stone_levels.append(next_stone_count)  # Append to the list

    return stone_levels  # Return the list of stones
```
